A Glimpse of the Abuse of Chinese Merchants in Outer Mongolia

▲The Chahar Provincial Government Submits a Report to the Executive Yuan

The Chahar Automobile Association has submitted a special report to the Automobile Management Office of the Provincial Government regarding the abuse of Chinese merchants by the Kulun government. The report states: "Since 1920, when Mongols colluded with the Russian White Army to capture Kulun, until the spring of 1921, the Mongols could not bear the oppression of the White Army, so they re-allied with the Red Army and drove the White Army out of Mongolia. Since then, it has become a Russian colony. The treatment of Chinese people was initially lenient, but then the conspiracy was revealed. The Far East Bank was created to issue banknotes and order Chinese merchants to be exempt from storing Mongolian currency and not to store foreign currency. If it is found, it will not only be confiscated, but also subject to considerable punishment. Chinese people are also not allowed to sell tea, tobacco, and alcohol. These three items are a major sales channel for Chinese people operating in Mongolia, so Chinese people have resisted more and more. Only alcohol is sold exclusively. As for the goods sent by Chinese merchants, they often pay one to six levels of surcharges. Currently, regardless of what it is, taxes are levied at a rate of 15%, and the taxes often exceed the original price. Chinese people in Kulun also have to pay head tax, passport tax, water tax, business tax, land tax, housing tax, etc., in various names. Furthermore, it is claimed that as many as six businesses in the same industry have been sealed up in the Wucheng area, three in the Eastern Village, and three in the Western Village. Furthermore, according to a guest from Kulun on November 13, a certain business had a turnover of 70,000 silver dollars in the first half of the year and was taxed 160,000. In the second half of the year, the turnover was still 70,000 silver dollars, and it was taxed 320,000. When the business questioned them, they said that if you do not follow this method, you can stop doing business immediately and sell it within a time limit. If the goods are not sold out by the deadline, they will all be confiscated." The Management Office believes that if the Mongol government treats Chinese people harshly, it will not only damage the automobile industry, but also cause great losses to the national tax revenue and the entire Chinese business community. Therefore, it has submitted a special report to the provincial government and forwarded it to the central government, requesting a way to provide relief. The Chahar Provincial Government believes that Outer Mongolia is the center of commerce for Rehe, Chahar, Suiyuan, and the three northeastern provinces, and is closely related to the livelihoods of the people in those provinces. Now that the Mongolian government is being induced and instigated by the Russians, and is abusing Chinese merchants in this way, it is not only the merchants in Mongolia who are directly oppressed and plundered, but also the domestic economy and people's livelihoods will be greatly affected. Therefore, it has submitted a special report to the Executive Yuan for review. After receiving the report, the Executive Yuan has, in addition to forwarding it to the National Government for consideration, also instructed the Ministries of Industry and Commerce and Foreign Affairs to investigate and handle the matter.

Reorganization of the Hubei Provincial Government Ordered

▲The Provincial Government Holds a Closing Meeting and Each Department Handles the Handover

▲Before the New Appointees Arrive, They are Still Responsible for Maintaining the Status Quo

Hankou Correspondence: Since the Central Army settled Wuhan last year and ordered the reorganization of the Hubei Provincial Government, the appointed members were He Chengjun, Fang Benren, Li Jihong, Xiao Xuan, Huang Changgu, Fang Juehui, He Guoguang, Peng Jieshi, and Xiong Bingkun, a total of nine people. The Department of Civil Affairs was established first, with Fang Juehui acting as the director. The Departments of Finance, Construction, and Education followed. Li Jihong concurrently served as the director of the Department of Finance, Xiao Xuan concurrently served as the director of the Department of Construction, and Huang Changgu, the secretary-general of the provincial government, concurrently served as the director of the Department of Education. Later, Fang Benren returned to Hubei and took office as the director of the Department of Civil Affairs and acting chairman. Then, a Department of Agriculture and Mines was added to place Fang Juehui. At that time, Feng Yuxiang raised troops, and the Central Plains were in turmoil. Chairman He Chengjun was in charge of the Peiping Headquarters and had no time to go south to take office. Acting Chairman Fang Benren was ordered to travel between Liaoning and Shanxi and had no time to rest. Xiao Xuan then acted as the chairman of the provincial government. However, after Fang left Hubei, the members differed in political views, and their opinions were quite deep. The political affairs meetings were suspended for a long time, and all facilities were inevitably suspended. When He returned to Hubei to take office, he was dealing with the war against Tang Shengzhi and went to Henan to supervise the army after a few days in Hubei, without any significant performance. Recently, He returned to Hubei and, in view of the dereliction of duty in Hubei Province, repeatedly telegraphed Chairman Chiang to request resignation and focus on military affairs. After Chairman Chiang earnestly persuaded him to stay, he dismissed the idea of resigning, and the reorganization of the provincial government was decided at the 215th Central Political Conference on the 5th of this month. It was found that in this reorganization of the provincial government, only He Chengjun, Huang Changgu, Peng Jieshi, and Xiong Bingkun were reappointed. The five who were not reappointed were Fang Benren, Fang Juehui, Li Jihong, Xiao Xuan, and He Guoguang. Wu Xingya, Zhang Guanshi, Huang Jianzhong, Fang Dazhi, and Xie Lü were newly appointed. Wu Xingya was also appointed as the director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Zhang Guanshi was also appointed as the director of the Department of Finance, Huang Changgu was reassigned as the director of the Department of Construction, and Huang Jianzhong was also appointed as the director of the Department of Education. The Department of Agriculture and Mines was abolished and merged into the Department of Construction to set up a section to handle it. As for the position of secretary-general, it has not yet been determined. After receiving the news of the reorganization, the provincial government convened a closing meeting on the 7th, attended by Xiao Xuan, Peng Jieshi, Xiong Bingkun, Huang Changgu, and Wu Jiantao, the secretary of the Department of Civil Affairs. Li Jihong also rushed back from Beijing to attend. It was resolved that each department would rush to close from today and prepare to hand over, but before the new appointees arrive, they are still responsible for maintaining the status quo. At the same time, He Chengjun was urged by telegram to return to Hubei as soon as possible. It is reported that He has replied by telegram, setting off on the 7th on the Chu You warship to the west. As for Wu Xingya, the director of the Department of Civil Affairs, he is still in Anhui and will not be able to set off until the director of the Department of Civil Affairs and acting chairman hands over. Huang Jianzhong, the director of the Department of Education, and member Xie Lü are still in Beijing and will also set off for Hubei soon. Zhang Guanshi, the director of the Department of Finance, and member Fang Dazhi are both in Hankou. It is expected that the reorganization of the provincial government will be completed in a week. (February 8th)

Transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway Telegraph Rights Issue

▲Liaoning Sends Li Deyan to Harbin to Negotiate

▲A Prerequisite is the Return of the Telegraph Rights

Harbin Correspondence on the 4th: Regarding the dispute over the Chinese Eastern Railway telegraph rights between China and Russia, since Li Deyan, the deputy director of the Postal and Telegraph Department of the Northeast Transportation Committee, came to Harbin, the idea of ​​both parties resolving the issue through meetings has been getting closer. Li Deyan, through the introduction of Li Shaokang, the Chinese director of the Chinese Eastern Railway, has met twice with Izmailov, the acting Russian director-general, on the 1st and 4th of this month. The results are summarized as the Russian side's opinion, which is quite agreeable to the method of holding meetings and not involving the Sino-Russian Conference, and that the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Northeast Transportation Committee will directly negotiate. However, the difference is still that the telegraph rights must be returned first and then negotiations, which is different from our side's proposal to negotiate first and then discuss rights. The Russian Director-General once said to Li that if the Chinese side returns the telegraph rights, the board of directors will order the Railway Bureau to send someone to discuss. All other sections are easy to say, and the Russian side will definitely give in. This matter is slightly contrary to the intentions of the Transportation Committee, and Li Deyan dare not make the decision, so he telegraphed Liaoning today for instructions. If the reply telegram is permitted, the meeting can be opened in Harbin next week. It is reported that the Transportation Committee recently telegraphed instructions to Li, which probably stipulate the scope of the proposal and can be divided into (A) Resolving the number of character fees for Chinese telegrams transferred through the Chinese Eastern Railway Telegraph Bureau, because there are few telegraph bureaus purely established by China along the Chinese Eastern Railway. In the past, commercial telegrams were collected by the railway newspaper room, and a certain amount of sovereignty fees were paid to the Chinese side per character. The rest was collected by the Chinese Eastern Railway, called transfer fees. If the Chinese Eastern Railway is still allowed to send and receive commercial telegrams, not only the sovereignty fee must be stipulated separately, but also the transfer fee must be reduced. This matter will be handled in accordance with the method of paying fees for the connection between state-owned railways and local newspaper bureaus. (B) Resolving the issue of automatic telephone assets. The original installation fee of the automatic telephone, the current depreciation fee, and the pure profit of the Chinese Eastern Railway's occupation over the years should be calculated separately, reduced, and fairly valued, and the Chinese side will pay the price. (C) Resolving the issues of business fees and line management for long-distance telephones from Harbin, Manchuria, Suifenhe, and through the line to Vladivostok. The Russian side's proposal is roughly the same, but their claims may be different.

In the midst of these telegraph rights negotiations, the Manchurian Telegraph Bureau was suddenly taken over by someone who did not allow Chinese personnel to enter and work. The reason is that when the Russian army retreated, the machines in the Manchurian station's newspaper room were searched and transported away. After the restoration of transportation, the Chinese Eastern Railway Telegraph Department sent Russian personnel with a quick machine to restore telecommunications and installed and used the old machine that had not been looted. In addition to sending train telegrams, it also collected commercial telegrams. This matter clearly violates the telegraph regulations and infringes on Chinese sovereignty. The director of the Chinese Telegraph Bureau then negotiated and planned to send personnel to enter and send and receive commercial telegrams. The Russian personnel actually refused and gathered many Red Party members, intending to fight. The Northeast Transportation Committee received a report from the director and ordered the negotiation to be carried out with the assistance of the military police. Commander Liang Zhongjia believed that his troops had not yet been fully reorganized and that strong enemies were in the territory and not far away. He feared that a rash takeover by force would cause another war. Therefore, he instructed the director to go to Liaoning for detailed instructions and then decide. Today, the director arrived in Harbin and reported to Li Deyan. In addition to forwarding the report to the Transportation Committee, Li instructed the director to wait temporarily in Harbin until the telegraph rights meeting was completed and negotiations were proposed. However, only train telegrams are currently being transmitted between Manchuria and Hailar, and telephone calls are also only connected to Hailar. After the Russian army destroyed the dedicated line for military telephone telegrams, the Chinese Eastern Railway has delayed repairing it. This line was originally stipulated in the Chinese Eastern Railway agreement as a dedicated line for the protection army. Our side also used it to send and receive commercial telegrams. Since it has not been repaired, commercial telegrams can only be sent and received by the Russian side, and military news is temporarily sent by post.

Heilongjiang Province Restores Border Patrol Posts

Harbin Correspondence: The establishment of patrol posts began in the early years of the Yongzheng reign of the Qing Dynasty. At that time, the intention of establishing them was that the border areas were desolate and vast, and there was no need to establish officials to govern them. Therefore, patrol posts were established in sections, and patrol officers and soldiers were placed to govern them. On the one hand, it was to defend against foreign enemies, fearing that there would be private carriers of boundary markers sneaking across the border to invade. On the other hand, it was to protect the border people, so that the population would be prosperous and prepare for the foundation of establishing counties in the future. Therefore, its system is the prototype of a county. Last year, the Sino-Russian issue occurred, and the Red Army often came to our coast to harass. The border patrol posts suffered greatly. All officers, soldiers, and people were either killed or captured. Those who were fortunate enough to escape all moved to other places. Now that the Sino-Russian incident has been peacefully resolved, Chairman Wan of Heilongjiang Province believes that it is necessary to restore the patrol posts along the Heilongjiang River. He proposed the provincial government meeting to discuss and resolve the rectification measures. The proposal is recorded as follows: "It has been found that the border patrol posts have been scattered since the military uprising. Now that order has been restored, efforts should be made to rectify them to strengthen border defense. However, it has been found that the border patrol posts have been established for a long time and have accumulated deep-seated problems. At the beginning of the establishment, there were general patrol posts and sub-patrol posts, and the unified system was clear and the response was still sensitive. Since each general patrol post was successively changed to a county, the sub-patrol posts still exist. Although they are nominally subject to the supervision of the counties under their jurisdiction, they are actually directly under the Municipal Preparatory Office. The patrol posts are far from the Municipal Preparatory Office, either thousands of miles away or hundreds of miles away. The reach is limited, and it is inevitable that they will be isolated when things happen. Therefore, each patrol post has become increasingly corrupt and is a mere formality. In the aftermath of this devastation, if we want to seek rectification, we should clear up the accumulated malpractices of the past. Now it is planned to restore the patrol posts in order. Each patrol post will have one patrol officer and ten patrol soldiers, directly under the jurisdiction of the county government. All foreign affairs will be handled according to the orders of the county government. In addition, a security squadron will be established in each county, under the command and supervision of the county government. The patrol officers and soldiers of each patrol post will also be directly commanded by the squadron leader. All matters related to peacetime training and management of each squadron and each patrol post, as well as the distribution of firearms, will be subject to the control of the garrison commander in each place."

Textile Industry Representatives from Various Counties Meet in Wuxi: This county has six yarn factories, including Shenxin No. 3 Factory, Yu康, Guangqin, 麇豐, Yeqin, and Zhenxin. According to the organizational law of trade associations promulgated by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, a place must have more than seven businesses in the same industry to organize a trade association. The Shenxin factory and others did not meet the requirements, so it was decided to jointly organize the Jiangsu Provincial Inland Textile Industry Trade Association with textile factories in other counties in the interior of Jiangsu Province. Last month, letters were sent to textile factories in various counties in the interior, inviting representatives to come to Wuxi to discuss and prepare for the organization of a trade association. Yesterday afternoon at 2 o'clock, a meeting was held at the Wuxi Textile Factory Federation outside Guangfu Gate. According to the predetermined order, Cai Jian, representative of the Wuxi 麇豐紗廠, was elected as the temporary chairman to pass the articles of association and discuss the association's affairs. The meeting was adjourned, and committee members were elected, with factories as the unit. Guangqin, Shenxin, 麇豐, Datong, Litai, Yu Kang, and Dasheng No. 3 factories were all elected as executive committee members. Immediately afterwards, standing committee members were elected. Cai Jian, representative of the Wuxi 麇豐廠, was elected. After the election, the association's affairs were discussed. It was decided to follow the methods decided at the last preparatory meeting, using yarn spindles as the standard. Factories with more than 25,000 yarn spindles would pay 300 yuan annually, those with more than 15,000 would pay 200 yuan, and those with less than 15,000 would pay 100 yuan. It was also stipulated that committee standing meetings would be held twice a year, in February and August.

Key Criminals Arrested in Xue Yan Bridge Robbery Case: In November of last year, the town of Xueyan Bridge, at the junction of Changzhou and Wuxi, was robbed by lake bandits. Three months have passed, and the case has not yet been solved. Recently, the Third District of the Water Police arrested Chen Fu'en, a key criminal in the case, in Suzhou. He confessed to robbing Xueyan Bridge Town. The Second District of the Water Police was immediately notified by telegram. District Chief Mao immediately dispatched detective Ni Gusheng to lead a team to Suzhou to escort him back for trial. It was also heard that on the 29th of last month, lake bandits took their hostages to Jia补, Zhejiang Province. While the bandits were on shore sipping tea, Wu Ruming, one of the hostages, pretended to go to the toilet and escaped ashore. At that time, the local security团 arrived in the town to encircle and suppress the bandits, who fled towards Si'an and Guangde. Wu Ruming returned home safely.

Theft Occurs in Tianxia Market: Tao Muguan's home, located at Shang陶 Lane, 533图, Bashi Bridge, Tianxia Market, Xixian County, was suddenly visited by ten bandits after 12 o'clock the night before. Four of them stood guard outside, and six broke into the house. They stole 13 silver dollars and clothes, causing a loss of about 100 yuan.

Changzhou

Opening of Long Police Training Class: Li Leng, the Chief of the Wu Yi Public Security Bureau, believes that many of the chiefs and police officers in the county's sub-bureaus lack knowledge. He is now planning to implement a long police training class, ordering the sub-bureaus to select active-duty chiefs and police officers to attend the training. Each class will have 60 students and will graduate in four weeks. The training will be completed in ten phases. All the instructors for the training class will be concurrently appointed by the Bureau Chief from the Bureau's officers, without any additional salary. The cost of opening the class has been budgeted and submitted to the County Administration Council for approval. Once the Financial Property Department approves it at its meeting on the 16th, it will be formally established.

Bian Dan River Tax Branch Robbed: The Bian Dan River branch of the Wu Dan Tax Office was suddenly visited by seven or eight bandits around 8 o'clock the night before. Three of them had pistols, broke down the door, searched arbitrarily, and fired shots as a warning. They robbed tax money, clothes, quilts, and other items, and went northeast by waterway.

Continued Trial of the Thirteen Gates Murder Case: The local court has been investigating the murder of Ding Yuxiang, a rickshaw puller, under the city walls of the Thirteen Gates north of the city. It has been learned that Shan Daiping usually had close contact with Ding and his wife, and his feelings for Ding's wife, Wang, were even deeper. There is no lack of suspicious clues. The Detective Team arrested Shan Da on Shan Lane Road and brought him back to the team. He is currently being interrogated.

Provincial Rectification Committee Investigates Tax Revenue: The Jiangsu Provincial Party Affairs Rectification Committee believes that the original intention of the revolution is to solve the suffering of the people and abolish excessive taxes. Therefore, yesterday, it specially ordered the Party Headquarters of each county to conduct a detailed investigation of the types of taxes, the number of people, the methods of collection, the approximate amount of revenue, and the general situation of local public funds and public property in each county, as a basis for studying the province's finances.

Qingjiang

Implementation of the Dismantling and Sale of the Qingyang Railway: There is an old section of railway from Qingjiang to Yangzhuang, built in the late Qing Dynasty. It was initially under the jurisdiction of the Sulu Company and was originally intended to be built from Qingjiangpu to Xuzhou to connect with the eastern section of Longhai. On the one hand, the history extended from Qingjiang to Guazhoukou or was built along the Fan Gong Dam to Nantong. Unexpectedly, the eastern section of Longhai later used the northern line, and the Guayang Motor Road and the Qingjiang to Gaoyou Motor Road were built one after another, resulting in the railway being useless and its largest income being only for transporting Xiba salt to the canal for shipment, with tickets that could be sold for more than ten li. In addition, in recent years, sea salt has been mostly transported by the Longhai Railway, and river transport has been entered into the river from Shanghai, coupled with the fact that the sleepers and rails have been in disrepair for many years, making the railway even more useless. Therefore, the current director of the Qingyang Railway Bureau, Zhang Maoji, recently sent a telegram to the Qing Bureau, ordering the station houses, roadbed rails, and old existing materials to be sold. On the 5th, the Bureau first sent workers to dismantle the white iron houses at the station, continued to dismantle the carriage houses north of the station, and then dismantled the rails and sleepers, along with the roadbed, one by one for auction. In addition, the Bureau has a lot of materials at Zhangjia Wharf outside Dongxu in this port, which will be sold together.

Truth About the 평 Garden Returning to Public Ownership: Regarding the matter of the 평 Garden in Xitang being taken back for public ownership and converted into Xitang Park, an investigation has found that when the 평 Garden in Xitang was initially created, it was built on public land. Last year, a person named Li Yunqing had a piece of land south of the garden and planned to build a house. He hired workers to build the foundation of the wall. At that time, the 평 Garden side came out to stop him, and the two sides started a dispute. Yuan Yuxin, one of the founders of the 평 Garden, beat and injured Li Yunqing's mother. She then went to the county court to verify the injury and accuse Yuan of assault, and also filed a case for the 평 Garden encroaching on public land. Seeing the trouble, Yuan avoided it, but the 평 Garden side, because the matter became deadlocked, applied to the Xitang District Finance Committee to transfer it to the county government for approval to be returned to public ownership and converted into Xitang Park for public viewing as a buffer to avoid litigation. They also drew detailed maps, measured the boundaries, and circled the land encroached upon by Li Yunqing, as well as the land next to the playground of the Second Elementary School, and submitted them to the county for record. Therefore, the county appointed a committee to manage Xitang Park, including Li Zhenwu and Yu Shenlian, totaling 11 people, and Yuan Yuxin was not added to the commission as a punishment. The Xitang District Finance Committee was ordered to transfer the order for acceptance and handling, and the case was resolved peacefully.

Examining the Xie Le Fang Murder Case: In Xie Le Fang, Xincang District, a carpenter named Wang A Liu, who had been blind in both eyes recently and could not work, cut down a small tree in his house for sale due to financial difficulties, earning 7 yuan and 2 角. Wang A Jin, a member of the clan, found out and argued with A Liu, wanting to divide half of it. A Liu replied that the tree in his house had nothing to do with him. The two sides argued. A Jin, with his violent nature, immediately went home and carried a pole, hitting A Liu's head randomly. Suddenly, blood gushed out, and he fell to the ground in extreme pain. He died from his injuries. The fang役 of the fang reported to the county, and personnel were sent to the countryside to examine the corpse. It was confirmed that he had died from his injuries. They immediately filled out the corpse form, prepared a coffin, and collected the body. At the same time, a telegram was sent to the water and land military police to strictly arrest the murderer.

Eyes Blinded by Quarrel over Gambling: Wu Zhu Ren, a farmer from Qitang Village, is fond of gambling. Recently, he has been setting up a牛場 and profiting quite well. The other day, he was gambling at a certain place in Xin Zhen Town and had a quarrel with a certain Wang from the town. Wang threw copper coins at Zhu Ren. The copper coin embedded in his eye, and blood flowed all over his face. Fortunately, he was persuaded by others to disperse. Shi Ren wanted to send Wang to the police, but was dissuaded by a certain gentleman. Zhu Ren's medical treatment was ineffective, and he is afraid of becoming disabled.

Educational News Highlights [L<

Ministry of Education Advises Provincial Governments to Effectively Protect Education Funding

The Ministry of Education received a report from the Education Bureau of Shaxian County, Fujian Province, stating that the county's established educational donations were stopped by the Finance Department's unilateral request, which had a significant impact on education. It requested that the Fujian Provincial Government handle local educational funds jointly with the Finance and Education Departments (whenever local educational funds need to be abolished or new funds should not be drawn, the Education Department should be consulted to ensure that local educational funds are not easily shaken) and effectively protect the Ministry of Education's maintenance of education funding, which concerns the whole country. In addition to approving and consulting the Fujian Provincial Government to effectively protect it, it recently consulted the provincial governments of each province, stating that the Education Bureau Chief of Shaxian County, Fujian Province, requested that the Fujian Provincial Government be consulted to jointly handle local educational funds and effectively protect them. The Ministry found that local education urgently needed to be developed, so it should broaden funding and increase protection. The Bureau Chief's request concerned the whole country. In addition to replying and consulting separately, one copy of the original report was enclosed, hoping that it would be noted and followed to emphasize education.

Local

Municipal Education Bureau Revises Regulations on Free Tuition for Students

▲Implemented from the Second Term of the 18th Year

The Shanghai Special Municipal Education Bureau recently instructed the municipal schools, saying that to comply with the order, the Regulations on Free Tuition for Students in Municipal Schools, which were ordered and announced in April of the 18th year, have been revised for the convenience of assessment. The revised regulations stipulate that each school should report the list of students receiving free tuition to the Bureau at the beginning of each semester, and all students receiving free tuition should be issued free tuition certificates for examination. The regulations have been submitted to the Municipal Government and approved by the Municipal Council, and copies have been issued for compliance. The Bureau will implement the regulations from the second semester of the 18th year.

Revised Regulations on Free Tuition for Students in Municipal Schools in Shanghai Special Municipality: Article 1: Students of the municipal schools who have one of the following qualifications may request exemption from tuition fees according to these regulations: A. Children of revolutionary martyrs; B. Students with excellent academic performance who are poor and unable to afford tuition fees; C. Children of current teachers and staff of municipal schools; Article 2: Those who meet the qualifications in item A of Article 1 must follow the Regulations on Free Tuition for the Children of Revolutionary Martyrs Promulgated by the National Government; Article 3: Those who meet the qualifications in item B of Article 1 must prepare the following procedures: The principal of each school shall submit them to the school affairs meeting for review and approval, and then report them to the Municipal Education Bureau for approval: (1) a pledge from the parent or guardian; (2) an application form filled out by the parent, relative, or guardian; (3) a guarantee form filled out by the guarantor; Article 4: Those who meet the qualifications in item C of Article 1, if they are studying at the school where their parents work, may be approved by the principal reporting to the Municipal Education Bureau. If they are studying at other municipal schools, their father or mother should fill out an application form together with a certificate from the principal of the school where they work and submit it to the Municipal Education Bureau for approval. Article 5: If a student receiving free tuition is found to have concealed or falsely reported information, in addition to suspending their student status, the principal shall order the parents or guarantors to repay the tuition fees they have been exempted from at twice the amount. Article 6: The number of free tuition students in Huna and Zhabei shall not exceed 10% of the total number of students in the school, and the number of free tuition students in other urban areas shall not exceed 15% of the total number of students in the school. However, this rule does not apply in special circumstances where the Municipal Education Bureau, after investigation, specially approves the exemption. Article 7: The students in each school who request exemption from tuition fees should submit a list of names to the Municipal Education Bureau for approval at the beginning of each semester. Article 8: All students approved for free tuition by each school will be issued a free admission certificate by the Municipal Education Bureau. Each student receiving free tuition should enter the school with the certificate. When submitting tuition fee reports, each school should send the free tuition certificates together with the reports to the Municipal Education Bureau for transfer to the Municipal Finance Bureau for verification (forms omitted). Article 9: Free tuition students in each school have the obligation to undertake the work designated by the school when necessary, and the general rules for their service will be formulated separately by the Municipal Education Bureau. Article 10: These Regulations will be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Special Municipal Government.

The Municipal Education Bureau announced that after the municipal and private schools in the city have completed their winter vacations and gradually opened, all superintendents and inspectors will set off to inspect and are currently allocating areas.

Municipal Guidance Committee for Further Education and Employment

The Guidance Committee for Further Education and Employment of the Shanghai Special Municipal Education Bureau held its first meeting on the 10th. The attendees were Xiong Wenmin, Ge Jiadong, Jiang Hongqi, Qian Weizong, Ni Wenya, Zhou Shang, and Ma Chong. Xiong Wenmin chaired the meeting, and Zhou Shang recorded the minutes. After the ceremony, the chairman reported that this committee was changed from the "Vocational Guidance Research Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Education Bureau" to the "Guidance Committee for Further Education and Employment of the Shanghai Special Municipal Education Bureau" and reported on recent work matters. The following was discussed: (1) Appoint Xiong Wenmin and Zhou Shang to draft the rules of the committee; (2) Appoint Xiong Wenmin and Zhou Shang to draft the implementation methods for guidance; (3) Pointed out the notes for guidance. Ni Wenya proposed that each level of school should set up exemption quotas, which should be sent by the committee to students with both excellent character and academic performance who are suitable for their personality after proper procedures to remedy the current abuses. Jiang Hongqi proposed that the Bureau should set up scholarships to create impoverished and ambitious young people. (4) The guidance methods should be stipulated by the Bureau and ordered to be implemented in municipal schools; (5) The scope of guidance was discussed and divided into this city and other places.

Nanhsiang Conference of Vocational Education Experts

The China Vocational Education Society held an expert meeting yesterday at Nanyuan, Nanhsiang. More than 20 experts attended, including Hu Chunzao, Gao Jian Si, Liao Maoru, Chen Qingshi, Liu Zhan'en, Gu Yinting, Zhao Shifu, Lei Binnan, Qi Yisan, Tang Tonghou, and Pan Yinge. Chen Zhongda, the County Chief of Jiading, and Yang Shizeng, the Director of the Education Bureau, also attended. After the ceremony, Jiang Wenyu, the Director, gave a speech. Liu Zhan'en, Liao Maoru, and Gu Yinting were then elected as the presidium. The following proposals were made: (1) Whether and how should spiritual training be implemented? After the proposer reported on the purpose of the proposal, Gu Yinting, Liao Maoru, Chen Qingshi, Gao Jian Si, Liu Zhan'en, Yang Weiyu, Lei Binnan, and Hu Chunzao expressed their opinions. It was decided to stipulate the standards and methods of spiritual training in vocational education, defining six standards: responsibility, work efficiency, mutual assistance, creativity, interest, and integrity. Concrete methods were then determined. The discussion then moved to proposals regarding vocational guidance. First, the director of the所 reported on past work. The following proposals were made: (1) Regarding the relief of ordinary young people who wish to work and study part-time, it was decided that young people should be self-sufficient. The current self-help student methods of Shanghai Jiang Vocational School, etc., should be adopted by each school as much as possible, increasing the number of student places and trying to run night universities and loan-based student aid. (2) The Guidance Institute should hire professors from various universities to organize subject-based guidance committees; (3) The guidance business should still advocate for measurement testing, first trying it locally, and then contributing it to society. Next, Jiang Xiangyu reported on the supplementary education run by the Society, which was extremely detailed about the vocational training schools, morning schools, and Tongsheng schools. All experts expressed their approval. The meeting then discussed issues such as agricultural education and industrial education. Experts expressed their opinions separately, which were extremely valuable. The meeting adjourned at half past four, and they took cars back to Shanghai.

Instructions from the County Education Bureau Regarding the Use of Temporary Funds by Various Organizations

Yesterday, the Shanghai County Education Bureau issued instructions to all education committee members, schools, societies, and organizations, stating that it is imperative to comply with the following matter. It has been repeatedly ordered that procedures for educational organizations within this county to access temporary funds require prior submission and approval before disbursement. However, instances have been reported of unauthorized transfers and disbursements without prior approval, as well as overspending and exceeding budget limits, which is disrespectful of the budgeting process. As the new semester begins, five articles are re-issued regarding the procedures for accessing temporary funds. Henceforth, should any school, society, or organization require temporary funds, they must strictly adhere to the specified procedures. Failure to comply with these procedures or meet the requirements will result in the Bureau's refusal to authorize reimbursement, regardless of whether the funds have already been spent. This order is issued for compliance and notification.

Recent News from the Zhongda Business School

Resignation of Dean Cheng Approved: Cheng Zhenji, Dean of the Zhongda Business School, has been concurrently serving as the Manager of the Hangzhou China Agricultural and Industrial Bank. Due to his demanding workload, he has repeatedly submitted his resignation to the university president, in order to focus on his duties. However, it was not approved until recently, when he was appointed as a senior advisor to the Zhejiang Provincial Government and felt that his responsibilities were too heavy to handle and that his duties would prevent him from travelling easily. Also, the completion of the school building project allowed him to lay down the responsibilities of his role and so a formal and stern resignation was submitted a few days prior and yesterday, the university president approved his resignation as Dean of the Business School and ordered all departments to expedite the handover process. It is said that the successor has already been appointed by the university president and will soon take office.

Scheduled Class Start Date: The school has scheduled registration and tuition payment for both new and returning students to begin on the 12th of this month and end on the 16th. Classes will officially begin on the 17th. Students who fail to return to school by the deadline will be considered late. After one week, returning students must provide a certificate from their parents, stamped with their official seal, explaining the reason for their absence. New students who still fail to register after this period will be removed from the roster in accordance with the regulations.

Expected Start Date for School Building Construction: The school has long planned to build new facilities, and the project has been actively underway. It has now been learned that the economic plans and drawings have been finalized and contract drafting and bidding will soon begin. It is expected that construction will begin in April of this year.

Following a meeting of the school affairs committee, it was decided to hold a transfer examination for first-year students yesterday (the 10th). Late applications will not be considered. Dozens of students applied, and a rigorous selection process was used, based solely on academic performance. The two-day examination concluded today, and successful applicants will receive notification letters within the next few days. No public announcements will be made in newspapers.

Sports

Actively Preparing for the Citywide Sports Meet

(1) Preparatory Meeting Today

The preparatory committee for the Shanghai Special Municipality Education Bureau's first citywide sports meet will hold its third meeting today at 4:00 PM in the main hall of the Da Zhonghua Restaurant on Zhonghua Road, near the Old West Gate in the Nanshi district. Important issues to be discussed include the registration deadline, sporting events, and division of responsibilities. It has been learned that as the sports meet approaches, the Education Bureau is expediting the preparatory process. In addition to the original 17 committee members, six more members have been added: Yao Gengkui, Pei Shunyuan, Sun Daosheng, Ling Xitao, Li Feiyun, and Zhang Guoxun. This expansion will help them collectively manage the event. The sporting events have already been finalized, and the standards for the awards will follow those set by the National Games.

(1) Citywide Sports Meet Regulations

Chapter 1: General Principles

Article 1: The purpose of this meet is to promote sports among citizens of the city, cultivate healthy bodies, and select representatives from this city for the upcoming National Games.

Article 2: With the exception of those whose profession is sports, all students from secondary schools and above, as well as members of the public, within this city may become members of this association.

Article 3: Members of this association may use the China Sports Field on Labor Shenfu Road.

Article 4: The dates for this association's meet are set for March 13th to 16th of the 19th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1930].

Article 5: This association will have a chairman, a vice-chairman, and a director of affairs to oversee all activities.

Article 6: The association's operations will be divided into two departments: administrative and technical. Each department will have a director.

Article 7: All competition rules for the track and field events, swimming, and ball games will follow the latest Far Eastern Games rules. This association may make reasonable modifications for special cases, but these must be announced publicly one month before the meet.

Chapter 2: Administrative Department

Article 8: This department will have six divisions: general affairs, accounting, documentation, editing, hospitality, and security. In addition to a director, each division will have an unspecified number of staff, determined by the director based on the workload. Separate regulations will be established for each division.

Chapter 3: Technical Department

Article 9: This department will have two divisions: competition and venue. In addition to a director, each division will have an unspecified number of staff, determined by the director based on the workload. Separate regulations will be established for each division.

Chapter 4: Miscellaneous Provisions

Article 10: These regulations will be implemented after being submitted by the City Education Bureau and approved by the Special Municipality Government.

(2) Sporting Events

▲Men's Division

(1) Track and Field Events: (1) 100 meters, (2) 200 meters, (3) 400 meters, (4) 800 meters, (5) 1500 meters, (6) 10,000 meters, (7) 110-meter hurdles, (8) 200-meter hurdles, (9) 12-pound shot put, (10) discus throw, (11) javelin throw, (12) high jump, (13) long jump, (14) pole vault, (15) triple jump.

(2) All-Around Competition: (1) Pentathlon (long jump, javelin, 200 meters, discus, 1500 meters), (2) Decathlon (100 meters, long jump, 16-pound shot put, high jump, 400 meters, 110-meter hurdles, discus, pole vault, javelin, 1500 meters), (3) 800-meter relay, (4) 1600-meter relay.

(3) Ball Games: (1) Football (soccer), (2) Baseball, (3) Basketball, (4) Volleyball, (5) Tennis.

(4) Swimming: (1) 50-meter freestyle, (2) 100-meter freestyle, (3) 400-meter freestyle, (4) 1500-meter freestyle, (5) 100-meter backstroke, (6) 200-meter breaststroke, (7) 200-meter medley relay.

Women's Division

(1) Track and Field Events: (1) 50 meters, (2) 100 meters, (3) 200-meter relay, (4) 8-pound shot put, (5) high jump, (6) long jump, (7) ball throw.

(2) Ball Games: (1) Basketball, (2) Volleyball, (3) Tennis.

Women's Open Basketball Game: Women's Western Youth Wins Over Qiangnan

▲Score: 24 to 15

The Qiangnan and Women's Western Youth basketball teams, both superior in the Shanghai Women's Open Basketball League, faced off at the Seafarers' Youth Association yesterday afternoon at 5:30 PM. A large crowd gathered for the event. The Women's Western Youth team won with a score of 24 to 15. In the first half, they led 13 to 4. The referee was Wu Bangwei.

Western Youth Takes the Lead: As the whistle blew, the intense battle began, with both sides firing shots but initially failing to score. After some back and forth, Qiangnan rallied and advanced aggressively. Cheers erupted as center Guo Xiaoping, with the help of her teammates, scored two points for Qiangnan. However, this joy was followed by disappointment as the accurate shots of the Women's Western Youth forwards quickly turned the tide. The Women's Western Youth forwards spent most of the first half maneuvering within Qiangnan's territory, relentlessly attacking. Qiangnan's guards defended strongly, but they focused too much on watching the players and not enough on the ball's trajectory, resulting in several fouls and lost points. The Women's Western Youth led 13 to 4 at halftime.

Qiangnan Shows Strength in the Second Half: As the second half began, Qiangnan had a successful start. Pei Geta of the Women's Western Youth team won the initial ball. After that, the Qiangnan players were very active, both scoring points and blocking opponents' movements. Qiangnan scored eight points in the third quarter, while Women's Western Youth only scored three. The score was still led by the Western Youth team at sixteen to twelve. At the start of the fourth quarter, it appeared that Qiangnan could muster their last bit of courage and reverse the defeat. However, their morale faltered, and they suffered a major setback. Although they rallied somewhat later, it was a spent force. As a result, the Women's Western Youth won with a score of 24 to 15. Their chances of winning the championship have now improved.

Local News

Reorganization of the Provisional Court: New Agreement

▲A Total of Ten Articles

The agreement for the reorganization of the Shanghai Provisional Court, as reported yesterday by the Nanjing Minsheng Daily, is reproduced as follows: (Article 1) The Shanghai International Settlement Provisional Court will be reorganized into a district court that fully conforms to the Chinese judicial system. (Article 2) The Jiangsu High Court will be added as the appellate body for the court, with the Supreme Court as the ultimate appellate body. (Article 3) A prosecutor's office will be added to the court as an investigative body. All prosecutors will be appointed and removed by the Ministry of Judicial Administration. (Article 4) Bailiffs and judicial police will be added to assist in the execution of civil and criminal judgments. (Article 5) Bailiffs and judicial police will be supervised and directed by the court and appointed and removed by the court. (Article 6) All settlement prisons should apply Chinese prison law. The Ministry of Judicial Administration may send personnel to inspect and supervise them at any time. Convicted prisoners, except for those who violate police regulations, may be transferred to mainland prisons for execution of sentences. (Article 7) The jury and advisory system is abolished. However, the police may send lawyers to court during trials. If the lawyer believes that a case is related to the police department, he may submit written opinions for the presiding judge to consider and adopt. (Article 8) Foreign lawyers must pass the examination and qualification of the Lawyers' Qualification Committee of the Ministry of Judicial Administration and obtain a lawyer's license before they can appear in court. When applying the law, they must comply with Chinese law. (Article 9) Whenever the court certifies that a person should be summoned or detained, the police should hand them over without delay. When other agencies detain a person, they must obtain special permission from the court after inquiry before they can detain them. (Article 10) The effective period of this agreement is three years. If there are any revisions needed within the three years, they must be agreed upon by both parties. After the agreement expires, it will continue to be effective if both parties agree. This agreement shall take effect from the date of signature by both parties. There are also three annexes.

The Municipal Council Does Not Have the Right to Judge Fines

▲Ministry of Justice Responds to the Taxpayers' Association

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Shanghai Settlement previously wired the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Judicial Administration requesting the correction of information published in the Da Wan Bao regarding the reorganization of the Shanghai Provisional Court, which stated that the Municipal Council could adjudicate fines under 50 yuan. The Association also sent letters to various groups to unite and fight for this issue. The Association received a reply from the Ministry of Judicial Administration and a reply from the Shanghai Special Municipality Merchant Association Consolidation Committee yesterday. The letters are transcribed below: (1) The Ministry of Judicial Administration wired, "The Shanghai Settlement Chinese Taxpayers' Association: Your wire received. We have investigated the information in that newspaper and found it to be untrue. Please do not worry. Jia, Ministry of Judicial Administration." (2) The Shanghai Special Municipality Merchant Association Consolidation Committee replied, "In response to your letter of the 8th of this month, regarding the Da Wan Bao's report that the new Provisional Court Reorganization Agreement would allow the Municipal Council police to adjudicate police cases violating Municipal Council regulations with fines under 50 yuan, which would undermine judicial independence and expand police powers, we have sent a telegram requesting rectification. The matter concerns China's legal rights and is not a minor issue. Our association has also requested the Judicial Yuan and the Ministry of Justice to promptly correct the situation. We are responding accordingly, please note."

Another Difficulty in Raw Silk Inspection

▲Jili Silk Is Not Suitable for Oven Inspection

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Office of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce will implement public weight inspection of exported raw silk (i.e., extracting silk samples for oven inspection) starting on March 1. Silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have encountered many obstacles in implementing this system and convened a joint meeting, publicly electing Huang Jinchen, Shen Huachen, and five other representatives to meet with Minister Kong and Director Zou to explain the difficult circumstances and request assistance. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that local Jili silk merchants believe that the public weight inspection of exported raw silk implemented by the Inspection Office includes Jili silk and local silk. Jili silk is known for its color, but its color will change after oven inspection, and the silk threads will become brittle. Modern overseas silk weaving factories use the latest high-speed weaving machines. If the silk threads are brittle and easily break, the machines will have to stop frequently to rejoin them, which is time-consuming and labor-intensive. Jili silk will inevitably be rejected, affecting sales to Europe. Therefore, representatives have been elected to join the silk factory representatives' delegation to meet with the heads of the Ministry and Bureau to request consideration of the merchants' difficulties in order to maintain the industry.

French Concession Promotes Stamp Tax

▲Foreign Ministry Office Sends Letter to French Consul-General to Negotiate

The Foreign Ministry Office in Shanghai sent a letter to the French Consul-General, Mr. Ganggelin, yesterday, stating, "Regarding the promulgation of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' 10th directive, we received a letter from the Ministry of Finance stating that the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau reported that since the stamp tax in the Shanghai Settlement was agreed upon and implemented, several months have passed, and the French Concession should follow the same procedures. On November 16th of last year, the Foreign Ministry was requested to instruct the Special Commissioner to negotiate with the French Consul, but no reply has been received, and the Jiangsu Special Commissioner has since been abolished, resulting in the suspension of negotiations. Please consult the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to continue negotiations with the French diplomatic authorities to implement the same procedures as the Public Concession. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs hereby requests you to investigate the previous case, continue negotiations with the French Consul in Shanghai, and report the negotiation situation as necessary. The letter of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs states that the case of establishing a bureau in the settlement to promote the stamp tax has been agreed upon with the leading Consul, and procedures have been established for implementation. The commissioner of the Foreign Affairs Office has informed your Excellency of this situation on December 20th of last year and requested your approval and notification to the police force. No reply has been received, and the Foreign Affairs Office has been ordered to abolish. Now, following the Ministry's order, we are continuing negotiations, and we are sending this letter to Your Excellency to request your approval to implement the same procedures as the Public Concession and to inform the Chief Inspector to instruct all police stations to promote the sale of stamps in the French Concession in order to increase tax revenue. We hope to receive your reply as soon as possible so that we can report to the Ministry."

The Old Baoshan City in Gaoqiao District is Not Military Property

▲ Request from the Land Bureau

▲ Explanation from the Municipal Government

Zhu Yan, Director of the Special Municipality Land Bureau, previously inquired with investigators from the Ministry of Military Affairs regarding whether the old Baoshan City camp area in Gaoqiao District should be considered military property, and submitted a request to the Mayor for review. The submission concerned whether the old Baoshan City in Gaoqiao District should be considered military property, and requested instructions. The case of the old Bao City being incorporated into the city's ownership was previously submitted, stating that the city had historically been a military camp. An order was received from your office to thoroughly investigate and report back for verification. Following these instructions, we consulted the Baoshan County Gazetteer from the eighth year of the Guangxu reign, which, in the section on establishment, states that in the second year of the Yongzheng reign, Governor-General Cha Bina and Governor Zhang Kai requested to divide the eastern territory of Jiading to create Baoshan County. It also notes that in the thirteenth year of the Yongle reign, Count of Pingjiang, Chen Xuan, requested to build a soil mound in Qingpu as Baoshan Garrison. After the county was established, the Wusong Garrison became the county seat, and Baoshan was adopted as the county name. The section on city governance mentions the city of the Baoshan Garrison east of the river, and also states that in the thirty-third year of the Kangxi reign, Li Jixun, Deputy Prefect for Maritime Defense of Suzhou Prefecture, oversaw the construction of the new city.

Baoshan City should be the new Baoshan Garrison city east of the river. Since it is named a garrison city and was supervised by the Deputy Prefect for Maritime Defense, it should belong to the Maritime Defense Garrison and be a military camp. The descendants of the garrison soldiers inherited it through generations, which should be the reason for their occupation.

However, the time of their occupation, whether reporting procedures had been completed before, and whether there had been any land contracts or sales afterward, are all undocumented. Instructions have already been issued to the municipal committee members of the Gaoqiao District to investigate in detail. Now, we have received your office's instruction No. 2355, which briefly states: "Approved the Ministry of Military Affairs' consultation to investigate undisposed military properties and requested to instruct all subordinates to assist accordingly." Therefore, a copy of the investigation district list is attached to order compliance and assistance, and special attention should be paid to the distinction between municipal and military properties during assistance. Following these instructions, this bureau should comply. However, regarding whether this bureau should regard the old Baoshan City as military property, except for the City God Temple, and inform the investigators from the Ministry of Military Affairs, this document is specially prepared and submitted for review. We request your instructions. After receiving the submission, the Mayor immediately instructed the bureau: "Noted. This case has been thoroughly investigated by this government based on past facts and history. The old Baoshan City has been detached from military affairs for over two hundred years and can no longer be regarded as a military camp. Moreover, the nature of a city with a history belongs to the military. Therefore, the land within the city is mostly tax-free, as is the current Baoshan County city, which was completely tax-free before the land survey. This is clear proof that the land was originally military-owned, and the occupants only paid taxes after the land survey and did not receive any compensation. Article 770 of the General Provisions of the Civil Code Property Law promulgated by the central government on January 30, Year 18, states that a person who has peacefully and continuously possessed unregistered real estate belonging to others for ten years with the intention of ownership, and whose possession began in good faith and without fault, may request registration as the owner. Therefore, considering the old Baoshan City, the possession has exceeded one hundred years, and the rights of the possessors should be recognized. It should be treated as public land occupied by citizens and should no longer be regarded as military property. When the Ministry of Military Affairs sends personnel to Shanghai for investigation, there is no need to notify them about this old Baoshan City. However, whether this city can refer to the example of the Baoshan city moat land and charge a fee as appropriate should be reviewed and reported by the bureau first, and then a decision will be made and instructions will be issued for implementation."

The Land Bureau Urges Payment of Winter Grain Tax

The Municipal Land Bureau issued a public notice on the eighth of this month, stating: "Notice regarding the conversion of grain tax fields in various districts of this Special Municipality. As stipulated by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, all grain taxes will be increased from the seventeenth year onward. Upon receiving the order from the Municipal Government, this bureau issued a public notice on March 11, Year 18, to start collecting the tax. The deadline has long passed, and the winter grain tax for the eighteenth year has already begun. However, the number of households paying the increased tax for the seventeenth year is still very low. Grain tax is a national tax, and the increase in grain tax for the conversion of grain tax fields in this city has been finalized. It cannot be arbitrarily delayed. Therefore, another earnest public notice is issued to all property owners of converted grain tax fields in this Special Municipality. They must pay the increased grain tax amount for the seventeenth year, along with the winter grain tax due this year, as soon as possible at the counter to obtain a receipt for their business. Do not delay any further, lest you be penalized. This notice is issued."

Coal Industry Cables for Expediting the Cangshi Railway

The Coal Industry Association sent a cable to Minister Sun, stating: "Respectfully to Sun Jun, Minister of Railways of the Nanjing National Government. Developing national coal is the sole source of China's economic strength. The Cangshi Railway is the vital artery for transporting national coal. If the Cangshi Railway is not built promptly, national coal cannot be developed, and further, China's financial leakage cannot be stopped, and China's economy cannot be saved. The key to success or failure lies in the urgency of the Cangshi Railway's construction. Today, China relies on foreigners for coal, with an estimated leakage of no less than 100 million yuan per year. Recently, due to the high price of gold and the low price of silver, coal merchants have suffered great losses, and transportation factories have also suffered hidden losses. The future of industry is declining daily, and the economic lifeline is suddenly filled with panic. Looking at the environment, we tremble with fear. The Cangshi Railway is truly the essential path to saving China from danger today. If the railway is built, the country will prosper; if it is not built, the country will be in danger. The Premier's instructions are clear to you. Please actively build the Cangshi Railway, complete it within a limited time, to open up resources and revitalize the national economy. We earnestly hope for your prompt adoption and implementation. The Shanghai Special Municipality Coal Industry Merchants Association kowtows, steamed."

Nanyang Tobacco Factory Closure Completed

The Nanyang Tobacco Factory in this port announced a temporary closure due to the gold price issue. Workers, suddenly unemployed, sent more than 20 representatives to consult with the company's authorities. After several days of negotiations, the two sides agreed after numerous meetings. Initially, it was agreed that each person would be given one month's severance pay. Later, the workers' representatives insisted firmly, and the company also raised funds in various ways. Finally, it was agreed that each would be given two months' severance pay, and wages for February 1st and 2nd would be supplemented. In addition, Assistant Manager Xu added a travel allowance of five yuan per person. The workers were generally satisfied. More than 90% of those receiving payments have already done so, and it is expected to be completed within about one or two days. Such a large factory, once swept away by the tide of gold prices, is a tragedy for the future of national industry.

News of the Maoye Bank Liquidation

▲ Partial redemption of banknotes to begin on the 20th of this month

The Zhonghua Maoye Bank, after suspending operations last May, underwent a five-month reorganization period without success. The Ministry of Finance, recognizing the importance of finance, appointed Xu Ke, Director of the Currency Department, on November 1st to supervise the liquidation. Liang Cihao, Qian Chengmao, and the American Su An were appointed as liquidators. Since taking over, they have handled matters very diligently. The organization established a general liquidation office, with branch liquidation offices in Shanghai and Tianjin. Each branch office is headed by a Chinese liquidator and a Westerner. The Shanghai branch office handles the Shanghai and Hankou branches, while the Tianjin branch office handles the Beijing, Tianjin, and Jinan branches. On the one hand, the Hankou branch is being closed and moved to Shanghai to reduce expenses. On the other hand, efforts are being made to collect debts to protect the interests of creditors and shareholders. Partial redemption of banknotes has already begun on January 20th.

▲ Commander Hu to go to Nanjing this morning to seek instructions

American Da Lai Violated Contract to Purchase Land

▲ Municipal Government Orders Cancellation

The American Da Lai Foreign Firm, previously under the name of Lu Da Lai, purchased land on Hongqiao Road in the interior of this city. The Land Bureau later found out that Lu Da Lai was actually a transliteration of Robert Todd Da Lai, the name of the Da Lai Foreign Firm. According to the regulations, foreigners are not allowed to purchase land except in areas approved for land transfers. Based on this, the Municipal Government ordered the Land Bureau to order the map broker, middleman, and landlord to return the original price and cancel the sale agreement. At the same time, a letter was sent to the U.S. Consul General in Shanghai, requesting that the Da Lai Foreign Firm be instructed to comply.

County Government Held County Administration Meeting Yesterday

▲ 32nd Meeting

The Shanghai County Government held its 32nd county government meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included County Magistrate Leng Jun, Chief of the County Public Security Bureau Zhu Chang, Director of the Construction Bureau Wu Wenhua, Director of the Education Bureau Shi Jin, Zhang Pengfei, acting Director of the Finance Bureau, and Wei Shuhan, secretary of the county government, and Xu Xiaochu, section chief. Liu Xuan, acting chairman of the county farm, attended as a guest. County Magistrate Leng acted as the recorder. First, the chairman reported that today's meeting was the 32nd meeting. In previous county administration meetings, the district chiefs had attended. It has now been found that the district chiefs rarely attend county administration meetings after reviewing the county administration meeting regulations and referring to the situations of other counties. Therefore, the district chiefs were not convened for today's county administration meeting, and district administration meetings will be held separately to discuss district administration. Next, the following cases were resolved: (1) Resolution to appropriately raise funds to construct long-distance telephones in various districts to facilitate traffic. It was resolved to first set up a long-distance telephone line from Maqiao to Beiqiao, and the director of the Construction Bureau was tasked with planning and budgeting the project and submitting it to the hall for approval. (2) Resolution to raise funds to expand the Minhang Tramp Vocational Training Center. It was resolved to retain it temporarily and discuss it again at the next meeting. (3) Resolution to prepare for the county's joint spring sports meeting for various schools. It was resolved to assign the Education Bureau to draft a detailed implementation plan and submit it for discussion at the next meeting.

Expansion of East Indies Dutch Vessels

Since the new vessels, such as the Dutch-operated Java Steamship Company's Chipada, were completed last year, the shipping routes from Shanghai to the East Indies have been greatly expanded. To date, it has been increased to four lines. The first route is from Shanghai to Hong Kong, Xiamen, directly to Batavia; the second route is from Shanghai via Xiamen, Lesser Luzon, to Surabaya, Bangka, to Balikoapan; the third route is to open from Shanghai directly to Balikpapan. The above three routes are scheduled to depart every fourteen days, one ship each. The fourth route is to travel between Shanghai, Xiamen, Hong Kong, Fiji, Bangka, Surabaya, Semarang, Batavia, and can connect with the Dutch Royal Mail ships for freight and passengers to Europe. Currently, the company has also agreed to add a new route to the port of Java, north of Java, from March 3, listed as the fifth line, and also connect Shanghai ships with various ports in the East Baltic Sea, listed as the sixth route, and also open a new route from Saigon in Annam to Shanghai, and has assigned three vessels, Norwegian, Eckler, and Zhijiani, to operate. Currently, there are five to six vessels arriving in Shanghai every month, and the largest business is the transportation of Dutch sugar to China.

Yangtze River Shipping News

Copper and Iron Increase Freight Rates: Taikoo, Jardine, and other six shipping companies convened a meeting of representatives of various companies yesterday to discuss the increase in freight rates for copper and iron. At the meeting, it was agreed that iron bars and iron plates, etc., transported from Shanghai to Jiujiang and Hankou, originally priced at nine taels and two mace per ton, would be increased by 15% to ten taels, five mace, and eight fen. Copper and purple copper, etc., originally priced at ten taels and nine mace per ton, will now be increased to twelve taels, five mace, and four fen. It will take effect immediately and has been notified to the passengers yesterday.

Jiang Tian Bids for Repair: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiang Tian vessel has been out of service since the beginning of April last year. It did not return to Shanghai until last month. After this nine-month suspension, the vessel's hull was already old, so there was a lot of damage. It would be difficult to resume commercial operations without a major overhaul at the factory. General Manager Zhao of the company convened a meeting of the section chiefs yesterday to discuss the repair plan. It was decided on the spot to solicit bids for the repair, and the Shipping Section was ordered to draft the bidding regulations and set up a bidding counter in the bureau, with the lowest bidder winning the bid. It will be announced immediately.

The Bureau of Social Affairs Distributed Saplings to the Public

▲ Can be collected during Tree Planting Week

The Bureau of Social Affairs of the city has opened a garden of more than 100 mu in Pudong, propagating seedlings every year, reaching about 200,000 plants. The number produced this year can already supply a part of the needs of tree planting. Recently, the garden drafted a method for the public to plant trees and submitted it to the Bureau of Social Affairs for presentation to the city government for review and implementation, planning to distribute 10,000 tree seedlings to the public free of charge for free planting. Therefore, all members of the public and groups and institutions in the city may register with the Bureau of Social Affairs the number of seedlings required and the planting location, and collect them during Tree Planting Week for self-cultivation, but must be responsible for protection. Within five months thereafter, the Bureau of Social Affairs will send personnel to the planting site to conduct inspections. If there is any arbitrary abandonment, non-cultivation, or causing wilting, the original cultivator must purchase seedlings for replanting. If it is confirmed that it is not possible to protect it by human force, causing the seedlings to wither, they must still collect them from the Bureau of Social Affairs, or replant them next year. The Bureau of Social Affairs shall, one month before the annual tree planting ceremony, conduct a detailed survey of the annual planting results, prepare statistics, and submit them to the city government for record.

Accused of Forging Checks to Defraud

Xiong Yuanchou, a native of Jiangbei, served as a accounting clerk at the Shanghai Securities and Goods Exchange on Sichuan Road and also ran a foreign goods business. Due to the failure of the foreign goods business, he was heavily in debt, and he forged checks to defraud funds for his use. Chen Gongbo, the head of the accounting department, discovered this and reported it to the General Inspectorate. Detectives were dispatched to arrest Xiong, and yesterday he was brought before the Provisional Court. According to the plaintiff's lawyer, Zhu Sifu, the defendant was in charge of checks in the accounting department, so he was able to fraudulently issue checks to withdraw funds from banks and money houses. It was not until the end of last year that the defendant's fraud was discovered, and the amount embezzled was silver 4,982 taels, 9 mace and 5 fen, and foreign currency 3,869 yuan and 7 jiao. He requested prosecution. When questioned, Xiong admitted the embezzlement. Judge Gao ordered the defendant to be detained pending sentencing next Monday.
